  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2967616309" />
    <a title="Norma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41400192-norma"><img alt="Norma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589038160p2/41400192.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2967616309?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Norma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Norma" href="/user/show/41400192-norma">Norma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41400192-norma?shelf=review-requests">review-requests</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2967616309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17770905584731799123"><b>Bewitching, creative, & magical!</b><br/><br/>THE TEN THOUSAND DOORS OF JANUARY by ALIX E. HARROW is an imaginative, enchanting, intriguing, and unique story that wasn’t the easiest book for me to read. I was a little bit bored in the beginning and almost called it quits quite a few times. I am so glad that I persevered because at approx. 58% in is when things started to get a lot more exciting and come together for me. <br/><br/>The writing is quite beautiful but extremely wordy and dense that definitely bogged down t</span>
  <span id="freeText17770905584731799123" style="display:none"><b>Bewitching, creative, &amp; magical!</b><br /><br />THE TEN THOUSAND DOORS OF JANUARY by ALIX E. HARROW is an imaginative, enchanting, intriguing, and unique story that wasn’t the easiest book for me to read. I was a little bit bored in the beginning and almost called it quits quite a few times. I am so glad that I persevered because at approx. 58% in is when things started to get a lot more exciting and come together for me. <br /><br />The writing is quite beautiful but extremely wordy and dense that definitely bogged down the story for me. I found that I needed total peace and quiet while I was following January on her journey to find those secret doors to other worlds. The writing style definitely distracted me from the actual storyline which was a shame because I absolutely loved this storyline.<br /><br />The details and workings of the doors was a little confusing for me as well. I felt it was left to our own imagination and devices......or I totally missed it! I had to channel the show "Supernatural" to help me visualize it on my own. Who knows if I got it or not.....but I'm satisfied. LOL <br /><br />I was going with three (3) stars for the most part but the ending definitely bumped it up to four (4) stars for me. It was an absolutely beautiful end to the story (that is definitely worthy of that beautiful cover) that gave me that warm fuzzy satisfied feeling that I seek and love.<br /><br />Thank you so much to Hachette Book Group for providing me with a physical copy!<br /><br />This review can also be seen at Two Sisters Lost in a Coulee Reading book blog:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com/">https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com/</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17770905584731799123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2866088741" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2866088741" />
    <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze"><img alt="Emer (A Little Haze)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390599p2/4629647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2866088741?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emer (A Little Haze)" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze">Emer (A Little Haze)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/44158423-the-ten-thousand-doors-of-january">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=all-the-pretty-covers">all-the-pretty-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=read2019">read2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=books-owned-all-formats">books-owned-all-formats</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=4stars">4stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2866088741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2034949972582545159">NOW PUBLISHED <br/><br/>The blurb from NetGalley:<br/><br/><i>EVERY STORY OPENS A DOOR<br/>In a sprawling mansion filled with peculiar treasures, January Scaller is a curiosity herself. As the ward of the wealthy Mr. Locke, she feels little different from the artifacts that decorate the halls: carefully maintained, largely ignored and utterly out of place.<br/>But her quiet existence is shattered when she stumbles across a strange book. A book that carries the scent of other worlds and tells a tale of secret doors, of love, adv</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2034949972582545159" style="display:none">NOW PUBLISHED <br /><br />The blurb from NetGalley:<br /><br /><i>EVERY STORY OPENS A DOOR<br />In a sprawling mansion filled with peculiar treasures, January Scaller is a curiosity herself. As the ward of the wealthy Mr. Locke, she feels little different from the artifacts that decorate the halls: carefully maintained, largely ignored and utterly out of place.<br />But her quiet existence is shattered when she stumbles across a strange book. A book that carries the scent of other worlds and tells a tale of secret doors, of love, adventure and danger. Each page reveals more impossible truths about the world, and January discovers a story increasingly entwined with her own.</i><br /><br /><br />This was a beautiful read. I was thoroughly enchanted by it. The story follows a girl called January... I loved this name for her because of its origins with the god Janus and how he looked both forwards and backwards, bridging doorways. <br />January's father travels constantly. He works for a man named Mr. Locke and is tasked with locating all manner of unusual objects and trinkets for this wealthy man. January is therefore left at home in Locke house where she is akin to Mr. Locke's ward... But her life doesn't feel as if it's her own. She feels like a fish out of water so to speak. Until one day she discovers a book about Doors between worlds... And her world is never the same again. <br /><br />I so enjoyed this story. It was simply charming. I do love books within books and this really had a great plot with how the "book within the book" ultimately connected with January's own story. The plot had everything I love; adventure, a quest, a love story for the ages, magic, secret societies, good guys, bad guys, a trusty canine companion... I was basically in heaven! <br /><br />January herself was a wonderful character. I loved how this book portrayed her as ultimately being quite spunky but at the beginning having her be rather more subdued echoing how she was being treated as Mr Locke's ward. Her character arc was very interesting to read about in how it explored how societal views on racial differences, pertaining to skin colour and wealth, affected January at the different stages of her quest in the novel. I also enjoyed how this book didn't shy away from upturning gender stereotypes and made the main female characters feel like incredibly authentic women who could be both soft and strong. These topics really added a sense of gravitas to the whole proceedings. <br /><br />This is the type of book that makes you long for the story to be real. I long to believe that there are doors between our world and elsewhere. That these doors can transport us to places that we couldn't even possibly imagine. Places that are exquisitely beautiful and yet ordinary at the same time. Places where people live lives entirely different to our own... And yet are entirely the same in that they share our need for love, family, companionship...<br /><br />'The Ten Thousand Doors of January' is a book for people who are still children at heart. People who want to believe in fairytale and magic. It's a book that really calls to mind that way that you feel about reading when you are a little kid; when imagination and story know no limits. I don't mean to say that the book or the story are any way childish but reading it just evokes that childish gleefulness of getting completely lost within the pages of your book. <br /><br />I highly recommend it to lovers of historical fiction who like a little bit of magical realism sprinkled in with the storyline. <br /><br />Four and a half stars <br /><br /><br />*An e-copy of this book was kindly provided to me by the publisher, Orbit/Little Brown Book Group UK, via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.*<br /><br /><i>
  <b>For more reviews and book related chat check out <a href="https://alittlehazebookblog.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a></b>
</i></span>

    <a title="Josiah Bancroft" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1328031-josiah-bancroft"><img alt="Josiah Bancroft" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510167829p2/1328031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2701451099?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josiah Bancroft" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josiah Bancroft" href="/user/show/1328031-josiah-bancroft">Josiah Bancroft</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/43517459-the-ten-thousand-doors-of-january">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2701451099" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3460889759125595408">THE TEN THOUSAND DOORS OF JANUARY by Alix E. Harrow is a beautifully written and absorbing tale of lost love, stately prisons, ghastly villains, and terrible secrets. It’s a smart and roving adventure that has a full and thumping heart.<br/><br/>Harrow has created a mythology that is both tangible and tantalizing, and has injected that vision into turn of the 20th century America. The historic details greatly enrich and never distract from a narrative that spans generations, continents, and worlds. This i</span>
  <span id="freeText3460889759125595408" style="display:none">THE TEN THOUSAND DOORS OF JANUARY by Alix E. Harrow is a beautifully written and absorbing tale of lost love, stately prisons, ghastly villains, and terrible secrets. It’s a smart and roving adventure that has a full and thumping heart.<br /><br />Harrow has created a mythology that is both tangible and tantalizing, and has injected that vision into turn of the 20th century America. The historic details greatly enrich and never distract from a narrative that spans generations, continents, and worlds. This is an ambitious, expansive story that never loses its sense of intimacy.<br /><br />Perhaps what impressed me most about THE TEN THOUSAND DOORS OF JANUARY was the inventive narrative structure, which incorporates texts within the text, weaving them together in compelling and surprising ways. <br /><br />This is a wonderful, insightful, and imaginative book. I highly recommend it, especially to fans of deft prose, historical settings, portal fantasy, and coming-of-age stories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3460889759125595408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2831311773" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2831311773" />
    <a title="Celeste" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste"><img alt="Celeste" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481055226p2/7317186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2831311773?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/43517459-the-ten-thousand-doors-of-january">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=portal-fantasy">portal-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=best-books-i-ve-ever-read">best-books-i-ve-ever-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=literary">literary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2831311773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3869359801462518485"><i>You can find <a href='https://wp.me/pa0WBY-vB' rel='nofollow noopener'>this</a> review and more at <a href='http://novelnotions.net' rel='nofollow noopener'>Novel Notions</a>. </i><br/><br/>Actual rating: way more than 5 stars.<br/><br/><i>I received a copy of this book from the publisher (Orbit/Redhook) in exchange for an honest review. All opinions expressed in this review are completely my own.</i><br/><blockquote>“Listen, not every story is made for telling. Sometimes just by telling a story you’re stealing it, stealing a little of the mystery away from it.” </blockquote><br/><b><i>The Ten Thousand Doors of January</i> is quite possibly the most achingly beautiful novel I’ve ever read, a</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3869359801462518485" style="display:none"><i>You can find <a href="https://wp.me/pa0WBY-vB" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> review and more at <a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a>. </i><br /><br />Actual rating: way more than 5 stars.<br /><br /><i>I received a copy of this book from the publisher (Orbit/Redhook) in exchange for an honest review. All opinions expressed in this review are completely my own.</i><br /><blockquote>“Listen, not every story is made for telling. Sometimes just by telling a story you’re stealing it, stealing a little of the mystery away from it.” </blockquote><br /><b><i>The Ten Thousand Doors of January</i> is quite possibly the most achingly beautiful novel I’ve ever read, and I find it mind-boggling that anything this lovely could possibly be a debut novel.</b> There are a scant handful of novels I’ve experienced in my life (<i>The Name of the Wind</i>, <i>The Resurrection of Joan Ashby</i>, and <i>The Night Circus</i> come to mind) that were breathtaking debuts of this caliber, and they remain my very favorite books I’ve ever had the pleasure of reading. <u>I’m so incredibly happy to add Alix E. Harrow’s novel to that list</u>.<br /><blockquote>“If we address stories as archeological sites, and dust through their layers with meticulous care, we find at some level there is always a doorway. A dividing point between here and there, mundane and magical. It is at the moment when the doors open, when things flow between worlds, that stories happen.”</blockquote><br />As soon as the synopsis and cover art (isn’t that cover almost painfully pretty?) for this book became public, <b><i>Ten Thousand Doors</i> immediately catapulted to my most anticipated book of 2019.</b> I preordered it for my birthday in February, even though it’s not scheduled to be released until September. Imagine my delight when, less than a week ago, I returned home from church to find an envelope featuring this book’s stunning artwork waiting for me on my doorstep. I’ve never received a more beautiful ARC, and this is the first time I have ever seen a galley delivered in special packaging such as I saw on my stoop. My husband laughed when I darted out of the car before it was even fully in park, leaving my phone and house key and everything else in the vehicle because I was so insanely excited. I tried desperately to pace myself, trying not to read more than 50 pages or so per day so that the book would last as long as possible. Alas, I was hopelessly incapable of sticking to that pace and found the story drawing to a close far too quickly.<br /><blockquote>“You see, doors are many things: fissures and cracks, ways between, mysteries and borders. But more than anything else, doors are change.”</blockquote><br />When you have such a high level of excitement going into a book, it’s very hard to temper your expectations and not be disappointed. And yet, <u>I never once felt disappointed in <i>Ten Thousand Doors</i></u>. <b>From page one, I fell in love with January Scaller.</b> When we first meet January, she is seven years old and, though her father is living, finds herself being raised by Mr. Locke, his benefactor, as her father travels the world, searching for exotic treasures to bring back to his employer. January is wild and sullen and headstrong and oddly colored, an unfortunate circumstance considering the time and place in which she lives. Worst of all, she’s imaginative. Throughout her childhood years, she is herded and tamed into submission by Mr. Locke and militant nursemaids, and sees less and less of her father. But though she has been bent by her benefactor, she has managed to remain unbroken, and finds many opportunities to test and marvel at the strength of her own character. <br /><blockquote>“I escaped outdoors (see how that word slips into even the most mundane of sentences? Sometimes I feel there are doors lurking in the creases of every sentence, with periods for knobs and verbs for hinges).”</blockquote><br />What I loved the most about January was how <i>alive</i> she seemed. <b>From the very beginning, she had an incredibly strong, distinctive voice, and an open honesty to her character that made her wonderfully believable.</b> She’s far from perfect, and that’s what makes her so engaging. <u>The amount of character development packed into less than 400 pages is astounding</u>. I loved watching this fiery little girl grow into a woman and recapture that spark that had been smothered within her. January has also been blessed with a trio of amazing friends who will do anything in their power to aid her on her quest. I don’t want to describe them and inadvertently take anything away from the reading experiences of others, so I’ll just say that they’re all three brave and loyal and steadfast, but in radically different ways. <b>I’m so impressed that Harrow was able to imbue even her side characters with such heaping amounts of personality and believability.</b> <br /><blockquote>“At this point, you’re thinking that this story isn’t really about Doors, but about those more private, altogether more miraculous doors that can open between two hearts. Perhaps it is in the end—I happen to believe that every story is a love story if you catch it at the right moment, slantwise in the light of dusk—but it wasn’t then.”</blockquote><br />Something else that I loved about this book was its duality. Though January is our protagonist, we also trek right along with her as she reads through a magical book that she found in an antique trunk. <b>The chapters of said magical book are very different in tone and voice than January’s chapters, and I thoroughly enjoyed this added variance.</b> January’s insatiable need to see how that story ended increased my own desire to continue reading. I felt that the author and purpose of the little book were both a bit obvious, but that they were meant to be so, which ensured that the predictability of that particular information couldn’t be in any way disappointing. <br /><blockquote>“If you are wondering why other worlds seem so brimful of magic compared to your own dreary Earth, consider how magical this world seems from another perspective.” </blockquote><br />Between the magical book and the otherworldly Doors mentioned in the title, I was strongly reminded of two books that I adore: <i>Inkheart</i> and <i>Every Heart a Doorway</i>. However, as much as I dearly love the two aforementioned titles, <i>The Ten Thousand Doors of January</i> surpassed them both in my eyes by intermingling the things I love so much about both. As with <i>Inkheart</i>, <i>Ten Thousand Doors</i> makes much of not only books but the words with which they’re crafted. And, as with <i>Every Heart a Doorway</i>, there are magical portals to a multitude of realms, hidden behind and beneath the mundane, and the search for these Doors is an all-consuming quest for certain characters involved. I won’t talk more about January’s Doors, as they are the backbone of her story and readers should learn about these portals as they read, but I love the entire idea of them and desperately wish I could find one of my own, and found them even more enticing than those in McGuire’s <i>Every Heart a Doorway</i>.<br /><blockquote>“Worlds are too complex, too beautifully fractured to be named.”</blockquote><br />Though I loved January and her friends, and I rooted for them as they faced down their foes, that was not my favorite element of this novel. And though the plot was everything I could hope for and more, keeping me enthralled and remaining at the forefront of my mind far after I had closed its pages, that was not my favorite aspect, either. <u>The thing I loved most about this book was the absolutely exquisite prose</u>. <b>Harrow is more than an author; she is a Wordsmith, a sorceress wielding a pen in place of a wand. Her writing is effortlessly stunning and unconsciously literary.</b> I’ve read a lot of literary fiction, and fantasy, and literary fiction trying to also be fantasy. I have found very few novels that managed to bridge the gap from literary fiction to fantasy in a compelling and convincing way, though I have found many fantasy authors who, in my opinion, can hold their own with any literary author. <b><i>The Ten Thousand Doors of January</i> is one of a mere handful of books that I’ve come across that could sit comfortably in either the literary or fantasy genre, and I think it beautifully combines both.</b> <br /><blockquote>“Doors, he told her, are change, and change is a dangerous necessity. Doors are revolutions and upheavals, uncertainties and mysteries, axis points around which entire worlds can be turned. They are the beginnings and ending of every true story, the passages between that lead to adventures and madness and—here he smiled—even love. Without doors the world’s would grow stagnant, calcified, storyless.” </blockquote><br /><b>Not only does Harrow have a gorgeous way with words, but she appreciates the building blocks of language in a way that I’ve rarely if ever seen in fiction. Something she did that I felt was incredibly unique was drawing attention to letters themselves.</b> When a word is important, you capitalize it. And when you capitalize a word, that first letter suddenly becomes a representation of that word. At least, that is what Harrow points out through the eyes and mind of January. For example, when you capitalize the first letter of Villain, doesn’t that V speak of daggers and fangs? That’s what January thinks. When you read this book, which I desperately hope you will, watch for explanations of words like Door and Threshold, Companion and Home. They were such beautiful ideas that my heart kept them, and I know they will come back to me every time I come across these words. <br /><blockquote>Worlds were never meant to be prisons, locked and suffocating and safe. Worlds were supposed to be great rambling houses with all the windows thrown open and the wind and summer rain rushing through them, with magic passages in their closets and secret treasure chests in their attics.”</blockquote><br />This is among the longest reviews I’ve ever written, and I still feel that I haven’t said enough. Or perhaps I’ve said too much. In either case, I hope I was able to convey how much I adore this book, and how deeply it touched me. <u>For the first time in my adult life, I’m honestly contemplating rereading a book immediately</u>, or at least within the same year. Maybe I’ll hold out until release day, and experience it again when I receive my preordered copy. I haven’t read a book twice in one year since I was in middle school. I can already tell that January is going to be one of my dearest friends, and that I’ll be revisiting her often. <b><i>The Ten Thousand Doors of January</i> is a marvel, and I can’t wait for the world to read it.</b><br /><br />The quotations in the review above were taken from an advance reading copy and are subject to change upon the book's publication.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3869359801462518485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2915234115" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2915234115" />
    <a title="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53419883-scarlett-readz-and-runz-through-novel-time-distance"><img alt="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600345081p2/53419883.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2915234115?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" href="/user/show/53419883-scarlett-readz-and-runz-through-novel-time-distance">Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2915234115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15718623785338837673">Upon reading the first few pages of The Ten Thousand Doors of January, it is pretty clear that Alix E. Harrow has a way to write most eloquently and organic, a whimsical tale reminiscent of childhoods' past imaginary wonders, curiosities, and secrets. The most beautiful, exquisite passages of words strung together so naturally, they elude to the calm and quiet brilliance within, ever so gently evoking the reader's attention wrapped around in every line, page by page.<br/><br/>The Ten Thousand Doors of Jan</span>
  <span id="freeText15718623785338837673" style="display:none">Upon reading the first few pages of The Ten Thousand Doors of January, it is pretty clear that Alix E. Harrow has a way to write most eloquently and organic, a whimsical tale reminiscent of childhoods' past imaginary wonders, curiosities, and secrets. The most beautiful, exquisite passages of words strung together so naturally, they elude to the calm and quiet brilliance within, ever so gently evoking the reader's attention wrapped around in every line, page by page.<br /><br />The Ten Thousand Doors of January is the coming of age tale of one girl's quest to find her past, present, and future behind doors that act as gateways to find her answers. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>"If we address stories as archaeological sites, and dust through their layers with meticulous care, we find at some level there is always a doorway. A dividing point between here and there, us and them, mundane and magical. It is at the moments when the doors open, when things flow between the worlds, that stories happen."</b>
</i><br /><br />January Scaller is seven years old around the turn of the last century when her story begins in Vermont, New England. Growing up on a large estate in the trust of Mr. Locke, a member of the Archeological Society. While her father is in his employ to gather interesting objects to add to Mr. Locke's collection of trinkets and artifacts, January longs to see her father more often and dreams of the affections of her mother. <br /><br />Raised by a German housemaid to give her needed structure in the day, she grows up with her studies and a love for reading and scribbling stories. Around the time the fog of adolescence lifts, she is confronted with her differences in social status and skin color, albeit being subjected to lectures in good manners all her years. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>"Power, my dear, has a language. It has a geography, a currency, and - I'm sorry - a color. This is not something you may take personally or object to; it is simply a fact of the world, and the sooner you accustom yourself to it, the better."</b>
</i><br /><br />January hadn't thought of her future much until she finds a leather-bound book written by her father. She discovers a story written in segments about someone's life that will most impact her self worth, her curiosity, and her longing to see her father even more. <br /><br />When January and an unlikely friend decide to pursue what they have learned of in the leather-bound book, the ranks of the Archeological Society will show their true colors and a sinister truth will come forth. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>"Do you want to leave?" I swallowed, tucking my fear away for some future time when I would be strong enough to look directly at it. "Yes," I answered and in answering realized it was true. I wanted wide-open horizons and worn shoes and strange constellations spinning above like midnight riddles. I wanted danger and mystery and adventure. Like my father before me? "Oh, yes."</b>
</i><br /><br />While January is told that her father has died, she has nothing left but to follow her heart and instinct. And when a sign from her father gives her a strong warning not to trust anyone, she has to make it across worlds through doors to find safety. <br /><br />A story in a story, beautifully imagined. An adventure of a different kind, most uniquely crafted and precious in details.<br /><br />***<br /><br />To read this novel was a breath of fresh air. I fell for the writing style and prose immediately. It's the kind of book I haven't read in a long time but that brought me back to happy times and places, where long summer days, running in fields, reading outside and childhood play was the most important thing in my life. <br /><br />While one travels in the book within a book, Harrow makes use of events in time and societal differences as reference points to imbue further a feel for its present and change, or the lack thereof. Exploring different worlds and ethnic backgrounds behind the doors and lives of others, it adds different views with an emphasis on family ties, strength, and love. <br /><br />Towards the latter middle of the book, the novel loses its tranquil tone, trading it for the action and deception that follows and crescents in turmoil to solve the mystery of the leather-bound book and January's race against time. Preferably, I could have continued reading more whimsical passages, but the scope and ideas were intriguing and became decisively textured more sharply. <br /><br />A special book you cannot go wrong with reading or gifting. So, add some lovely magic to your book diet and enjoy the world of Ten Thousand Doors... <br /><br />***<br /><br /><i>I received a digital copy of this novel from Netgalley in exchange for my honest opinion. <br />Thank you kindly to the publisher. </i><br /><br />Other reviews of mine can be found here:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://scarlettreadzandrunz.com/">https://scarlettreadzandrunz.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15718623785338837673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3360359206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9314109253903010612">I had avoided reading this book for months because of the hype and the fear of being disappointed, but then the library had it in stock, and it has such a pretty cover, and I could not help myself so I brought it home.<br/><br/>And I loved it! I always enjoy a good portal story and this one had so many portals going to so many different places that I gave up trying to work out where they went and why. I just let myself be swept away by the story and the extremely well written prose. <br/><br/>I thought the characte</span>
  <span id="freeText9314109253903010612" style="display:none">I had avoided reading this book for months because of the hype and the fear of being disappointed, but then the library had it in stock, and it has such a pretty cover, and I could not help myself so I brought it home.<br /><br />And I loved it! I always enjoy a good portal story and this one had so many portals going to so many different places that I gave up trying to work out where they went and why. I just let myself be swept away by the story and the extremely well written prose. <br /><br />I thought the characters were well done, especially the trio of January, Samuel and Bad. My main fear in this story came from constantly worrying about Bad. Of course there was more suspense than that and the last section of the book really ramps up the action. <br /><br />By the end there are moments to cry over and moments that had me sitting on the edge of my seat. There is also an entirely satisfactory ending. Very well done indeed and I will be looking out for this author's future work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9314109253903010612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3339931746" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3339931746" />
    <a title="Nataliya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya"><img alt="Nataliya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605995014p2/3672777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3339931746?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nataliya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nataliya" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya">Nataliya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/43517459-the-ten-thousand-doors-of-january">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=hugo-nebula">hugo-nebula</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3339931746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2636179809835614207"><blockquote>
  <i>“You see, doors are many things: fissures and cracks, ways between, mysteries and borders. But more than anything else, doors are change. When things slip through them, no matter how small or brief, change trails them like porpoises following a ship’s wake.”</i>
</blockquote>This is a story about the desire for unknown, the longing for change. It is a story of the dangers of complacency, blind obedience, unquestioning submission to those who proclaim they are the strong ones. This is a story of the need to ta</span>
  <span id="freeText2636179809835614207" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“You see, doors are many things: fissures and cracks, ways between, mysteries and borders. But more than anything else, doors are change. When things slip through them, no matter how small or brief, change trails them like porpoises following a ship’s wake.”</i>
</blockquote>This is a story about the desire for unknown, the longing for change. It is a story of the dangers of complacency, blind obedience, unquestioning submission to those who proclaim they are the strong ones. This is a story of the need to take action, to rise above what has been determined for you and do what you have to do regardless of the obstacles in your path. It is a story of growing up while holding on to curiosity and adventure which do not need to give way to propriety and stuffiness. It’s a story of family and abandonment. It is a story of how it feels to be the “other”, <i> “an in-between sort of thing.”</i><br><br>This is also a story about the power of words.<blockquote>
  <i>“If one follows the stories, one will nearly always find a doorway buried at their roots.”<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1590522807i/29546263._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>“Worlds were never meant to be prisons, locked and suffocating and safe. Worlds were supposed to be great rambling houses with all the windows thrown open and the wind and summer rain rushing through them, with magic passages in their closets and secret treasure chests in their attics. […]<br>I was so very tired of locked doors.” </i>
</blockquote>There are doors in the world — <b>or Doors, really</b> — that appear in the places where boundaries between worlds are thin and that can take you through to places that are different and strange. They allow for things unusual and new to flow between worlds, changing status quo, bringing fresh beginning with them. <br><br><b>But those Doors are closing now. Or rather, someone has been closing them. </b><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1590523373i/29546281._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>In 1901, January Scaller is seven. An “oddly colored” reddish-skinned girl, she is a ward of Cornelius Locke, a rich man, a no-nonsense member of an archaeological society and her father’s employer. January has no mother, and her father is always away on Ms. Locke’s archaeological expeditions, returning from time to time with a wealth of strange things that go straight in Mr. Locke’s vast collections. January is lonely, and resentful of her mostly absent father, and works really hard to earn approval and love from the replacement father figure, her guardian Mr. Locke who buys her things and takes her on long travels — and in return expects her to grow into a respectable young lady with certainly no penchants for imaginary things and wanderlust.<br><br>But then, at age seven, January walks through a blue Door standing in an empty field and sees a different world - one full of smell of ocean and blue water, one that calls to her. And eventually she notes that writing some things down when she really believes them makes them happen. But that is certainly nonsense, and no proper young ladies should be given to such flights of fancy. <br><blockquote>
  <i>“There was no room, it turned out, for little girls who wandered off the edge of the map and told the truth about the mad, impossible things they found there.”</i>
</blockquote>Then, at the age of seventeen, January runs afoul of those in power who view her either as a nuisance or an irritation to be swatted away. Those who look at her and see a weak colored girl of no consequence — unless she has something that they want. And January, sheltered and naive, raised to be quiet and pliable and proper, has a rude and abrupt awakening. <br><blockquote>
  <i>“The truth is that the powerful come for the weak, whenever and wherever they like. Always have, always will.”</i>
</blockquote><br>This book made me quite angry at times — angry at blatant power imbalances, at the injustice, at imperialism and prejudice - and at January herself — at her questionable choices and desperate desire to cling to normalcy, as abnormal as that normalcy can be. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Although it does turn out that there was a reason for her infuriating indecisiveness and desire to obey and please — for those obsessed with opening Doors, a Locke is a terrible idea. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And anger is often what fuels change.<b> And change, while not always good or bad, is what fuels and sustains life, even if it is inconvenient to the ones happy with status quo.</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>“The will to be polite, to maintain civility and normalcy, is fearfully strong. I wonder sometimes how much evil is permitted to run unchecked simply because it would be rude to interrupt it.”</i>
</blockquote><br>It is a well-written book, full of wondrous and magical things and told in a crisp well-crafted prose, with excellent plot and well-crafted characters, and enough worldbuilding to sustain sequels (although in this world of never-ending series I’m very happy with stand-alone novels). Its magical yet grounded, charming yet tough. It allows for a bit of moral ambiguity in the characters, with no one <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[except for Samuel, probably the weakest of the “good guys” <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> coming out of this smelling like roses. For a debut especially, it’s very strong; it reads as though written by a seasoned author, which bodes quite well for Harrow’s future works. <b>Those Hugo and Nebula nominations are well-earned.</b><br><blockquote>
  <i> “I hope you will find the cracks in the world and wedge them wider, so the light of other suns shines through; I hope you will keep the world unruly, messy, full of strange magics; I hope you will run through every open Door and tell stories when you return.”</i>
</blockquote><b> 4.5 <s>stars</s> keys to all the locked Doors.</b><br>———————<br><br>My Hugo and Nebula Awards Reading Project 2020: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3295830569">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2636179809835614207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2949697538" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2949697538" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2949697538?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2949697538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5893414276062224106">reading this book was like experiencing something gorgeous and beautiful and aching. I fully admire the writing and wanted to save half a million quotes. It also gave me strong flashbacks to things like Narnia (my whole childhood was Narnia so this story was such an adult homecoming) and also <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28449207.Strange_the_Dreamer__Strange_the_Dreamer___1_' title='Strange the Dreamer (Strange the Dreamer, #1) by Laini Taylor' rel='nofollow noopener'>Strange the Dreamer</a>, utterly and fully. If you love Strange, <i>do</i> try this. I think the strength of this book was the prose first, characters second. And it always takes me a little while to settle into the h</span>
  <span id="freeText5893414276062224106" style="display:none">reading this book was like experiencing something gorgeous and beautiful and aching. I fully admire the writing and wanted to save half a million quotes. It also gave me strong flashbacks to things like Narnia (my whole childhood was Narnia so this story was such an adult homecoming) and also <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28449207.Strange_the_Dreamer__Strange_the_Dreamer___1_" title="Strange the Dreamer (Strange the Dreamer, #1) by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Strange the Dreamer</a>, utterly and fully. If you love Strange, <i>do</i> try this. I think the strength of this book was the prose first, characters second. And it always takes me a little while to settle into the hum and flow of adult lit. But it was like this gorgeous, frothy and intricately frosted cake you have to eat with reverence. (I want to write this beautifully someday.)<br /><br />I do prefer character-driven books though, so in that regard I always found January less of a compelling heroine (also team Samuel-deserved-better-absolutely-the-whole-time) and I constantly wanted more and more of the side characters. (Ade and Yule were my HEART.)<br /><br />It also had thoughtful and hurting discussions on the injustice of misused power, colonialism, racism, the corruption of old white men who think everything belongs to them, and how women were called hysterical and mentally ill in the 19th century for daring to have a personality. <i>Be a good girl</i>...you just want to crush ink in Locke's eye honestly. (I researched, but I don't believe it's #ownvoices for the biracial rep, but it was very heavily <i>about</i> being biracial, so...that left me unsure sometimes.)<br /><br />This is full of Doors and worlds so different, but similar to ours, and gah, I love that. It's enchanting. I wanted more in all the worlds though, less in ours. And the style was stories within stories, so it was like 80% being <i>told</i> instead of experiencing it which...is a style. So I try to just appreciate the book for what it was.<br /><br /><b>Definitely a slow and whimsical story that unpacks how women are so often reduced to being powerless and how it feels to fight back, find your feet, and start yelling <i>or screaming</i> if that's what it takes. It's about searching for home. Finding your people. True love. And it's about the magic of words.</b><br /><br />I also lowkey had to read this in January for OBVIOUS REASONS.<br /><br /><br /><blockquote>"Because I didn't want to be safe, I suppose. I wanted to be dangerous, to find my own power and write it on the world."<br /><br />Perhaps I keep writing because I was raised in a world where words have power, where curves and spirals of ink adorn sails and skin, where a sufficiently talented word-worker might reach out and remake her world. Perhaps I cannot believe words are entirely powerless, even here.<br /><br />Worlds were never meant to be prisons, locked and suffocating and safe. Worlds were supposed to be great rambling houses with all the windows thrown open and the wind and summer rain rushing through them, with magic passages in their closets and secret treasure chests in their attics.<br /><br />I hope you will find the cracks in the world and wedge them wider, so the light of other suns shines through; I hope you will keep the world unruly, messy, full of strange magics; I hope you will run through every open Door and tell stories when you return.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="5893414276062224106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2849696726" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2849696726" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2849696726?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" href="/user/show/54886546-lindsay---traveling-sisters-book-reviews">Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54886546-lindsay---traveling-sisters-book-reviews?shelf=physical-from-publisher">physical-from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54886546-lindsay---traveling-sisters-book-reviews?shelf=traveling-sister-read">traveling-sister-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2849696726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17057745753179357009">3 stars. A spellbinding, imaginative, unique journey!<br/><br/>This novel is a creative, haunting and original story. The main character, January, is a young girl who finds a magical book that takes her on a journey through hidden doors into other worlds. In search of her family and of herself, January tries to piece together her past.<br/><br/>Based on the synopsis, I knew this was a bit of a risky read, but I wanted to take the plunge and try something outside of my usual genre. The first half of the book was int</span>
  <span id="freeText17057745753179357009" style="display:none">3 stars. A spellbinding, imaginative, unique journey!<br /><br />This novel is a creative, haunting and original story. The main character, January, is a young girl who finds a magical book that takes her on a journey through hidden doors into other worlds. In search of her family and of herself, January tries to piece together her past.<br /><br />Based on the synopsis, I knew this was a bit of a risky read, but I wanted to take the plunge and try something outside of my usual genre. The first half of the book was intriguing and exciting, however, my connection began to fade and confusion set in around the halfway point. My mind just doesn’t “go there”. I am not a fantasy or magical realism reader so this is a matter of me simply not being the right target audience for this novel. <br /><br />The writing was excellent. I loved the characters and thought they were entertaining and endearing. The storyline simply didn’t work for me. Please check out the many raving reviews from others who are more comfortable in this genre and can provide better insight.<br /><br />This was a Traveling Sister read with Norma and Brenda. We were happy to have had the chance to step outside of our comfort zone to read this together. <br /><br />Thank you to Hachette Book Group for providing me with a physical copy to read and review!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17057745753179357009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Portals and the multiverse and word magic and fascinating women and crisp, textured prose I wanted to fold and unfold like a letter. It's truly one of those books that's bigger on the inside, a house with countless rooms.</span>

<div id="review_2979629577" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2979629577" />
    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2979629577?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamad" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad">Hamad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=good-covers">good-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=from-the-publisher">from-the-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2979629577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9686002933140123862"><a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/10/03/the-ten-thousand-doors-of-january-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Review</a> ✍️ <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blog</a> 📖 <a href='https://twitter.com/Hamad9626' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href='https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> 📷<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “How fitting, that the most terrifying time in my life should require me to do what I do best: escape into a book.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>🌟 Disclaimer: ARC provided by the publisher in exchange of an honest review!<br/><br/>🌟 I am not a big fan of history in general and it was always my least favorite subject in school. I found that the same applies to the bookish world and that I am not a big fan of historical fiction. I saw someone describing this as historical fantasy </span>
  <span id="freeText9686002933140123862" style="display:none"><a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/10/03/the-ten-thousand-doors-of-january-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">This Review</a> ✍️ <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> 📖 <a href="https://twitter.com/Hamad9626" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> 📷<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “How fitting, that the most terrifying time in my life should require me to do what I do best: escape into a book.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />🌟 Disclaimer: ARC provided by the publisher in exchange of an honest review!<br /><br />🌟 I am not a big fan of history in general and it was always my least favorite subject in school. I found that the same applies to the bookish world and that I am not a big fan of historical fiction. I saw someone describing this as historical fantasy and I was intrigued! Like one of my most favorite things combined with my least favorite subject. Where would this combination lead to and it looks like there are a ten thousand doors that it can lead to.<br /><br />🌟 I was seeing 5 stars after 5 stars for this book and that made my curiosity peek even more! I requested an ARC from the publisher and I was provided with a hardcover!!! I still can’t get over that! The level of attention to details and aesthetics in this book is astounding. From the cover design to the chapters headers and more.<br /><br />🌟 The first thing that I noticed when I was reading is the writing style, Alex definitely has a magical prose that is fitting for a story of this kind! I was bored at some points and I will explain more on that later but the prose was what made me continue and I did not regret it. There was a change in the narrative voice at some points and it was intentional and I like how the characters pointed it out!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “It is at the moments when the doors open, when things flow between the worlds, that stories happen.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />🌟 All the talk about doors and portals made me -and other readers- get the “Every heart a doorway” vibes which is a great hit by Seanan McGuire. I like that series but I assure you that this is totally different and they may share only few superficial similarities. I said at the beginning that I am not a fan of historical fiction and that’s because I am usually bored while reading it. There were like 2 stories in one here and they fuse into one bigger story at the end. I may have been bothered a little bit by this because there was a difference in my interest between them. One of my friends was enjoying the book but when the second story began he lost interest and DNF the book!!<br /><br />🌟 The characters are well written and I liked how things turned out toward the end and I felt that I should have made connections earlier in the story but I missed them and was surprised in a good way!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “Books are Doors and I wanted out.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />🌟 Summary and Prescription: This is a book with a very beautiful prose for those who like magical writing. I would say the fantasy parts were not large and it reads more like an interesting historical fiction. I still like the description Historical Fantasy so if it sounds like something you would enjoy, don’t hesitate to give the book a try.<br /><br />You can get more books from <a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/?a_aid=2611996" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9686002933140123862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2890783312" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2890783312" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2890783312?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2019-shelf">2019-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=worldbuilding-sf">worldbuilding-sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2890783312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer124885838085288969">Like the cover to this book, the innards are lush, romantic, and adventuresome. Beautiful prose, much better story, and ten thousand open doors to other realms awaiting us.<br/><br/>Eventually. The first part reads mostly like a Secret Garden type story, complete with the right time period. This may be a bonus to a lot of you, but to me, it was quite simply okay.<br/><br/>When we get word of her father's demise, however, everything picks up pace. I particularly loved how vast swaths of plot were wrapped up in neat </span>
  <span id="freeText124885838085288969" style="display:none">Like the cover to this book, the innards are lush, romantic, and adventuresome. Beautiful prose, much better story, and ten thousand open doors to other realms awaiting us.<br /><br />Eventually. The first part reads mostly like a Secret Garden type story, complete with the right time period. This may be a bonus to a lot of you, but to me, it was quite simply okay.<br /><br />When we get word of her father's demise, however, everything picks up pace. I particularly loved how vast swaths of plot were wrapped up in neat lyrical bows, how other subplots were either supplanted, charmingly, or given a rich kiss before returning to the main thread. <br /><br />But what is it about, you ask?<br /><br />Not, precisely, about imagination and books... but THROUGH the books, or rather word-magic, through half-seen doors will we fly. Alternate realities, perhaps timelines, brutal places, rich places, and in them all, January quests. <br /><br />It is about family. <br /><br />And I admit I did more than tear up a little at the end. It was particularly gorgeous.</span>
  <a data-text-id="124885838085288969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3505714579" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3505714579" />
    <a title="ELLIAS (elliasreads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13699205-ellias-elliasreads"><img alt="ELLIAS (elliasreads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580549084p2/13699205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3505714579?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ELLIAS (elliasreads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ELLIAS (elliasreads)" href="/user/show/13699205-ellias-elliasreads">ELLIAS (elliasreads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13699205-ellias-elliasreads?shelf=2020-books">2020-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13699205-ellias-elliasreads?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3505714579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10962101103178820591"><b>
  <i>The Starless Sea met Inkheart, fell in love, and had a ripe baby. This ripe book is that baby.</i>
</b> <br/><br/>This book had some great incredible concepts that I actually wish the Starless Sea had incorporated into its own story. A story of loss, identity, and what it means to be a family. There were some things that irked me though— mc being indecisive and contradicting to her decisions, internalized colorism, certain character actions/choices that were a certain degree, so stupid. But—<br/><br/>— books about books</span>
  <span id="freeText10962101103178820591" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>The Starless Sea met Inkheart, fell in love, and had a ripe baby. This ripe book is that baby.</i>
</b> <br /><br />This book had some great incredible concepts that I actually wish the Starless Sea had incorporated into its own story. A story of loss, identity, and what it means to be a family. There were some things that irked me though— mc being indecisive and contradicting to her decisions, internalized colorism, certain character actions/choices that were a certain degree, so stupid. But—<br /><br />— books about books, doorways, other elseworlds, magic. <br /><br />Almost perfect.<br /><br /><b>Borderline 3.75/4 stars.</b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3011416068" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3011416068" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3011416068?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3011416068" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14010376624850245222">"There's only one way to run away from your own story, and that's to sneak into someone else's."<br/><br/><b>
  <i>The Ten Thousand Doors of January</i>
</b> is a wild, magical, fascinating story about incredible journeys, love, family, loss, and loyalty.<br/><br/>At the turn of the 20th century January Scaller is a young, curious girl whose father travels for business, hunting the world for antiquities and oddities, so he leaves her in the care of his employer, the eccentric collector of artifacts, Mr. Locke. Locke treats Janua</span>
  <span id="freeText14010376624850245222" style="display:none">"There's only one way to run away from your own story, and that's to sneak into someone else's."<br /><br /><b>
  <i>The Ten Thousand Doors of January</i>
</b> is a wild, magical, fascinating story about incredible journeys, love, family, loss, and loyalty.<br /><br />At the turn of the 20th century January Scaller is a young, curious girl whose father travels for business, hunting the world for antiquities and oddities, so he leaves her in the care of his employer, the eccentric collector of artifacts, Mr. Locke. Locke treats January with some indulgence until he realizes she has a wild spirit that requires taming.<br /><br />One day she finds a door in the middle of an abandoned field. When she steps through the door she finds herself in an entirely different world, a phenomenon she can hardly explain. Yet when she does try to share her find with Locke, she doesn’t understand the vehemence of his reaction or the punishment that follows.<br /><br />Of course, when you are forbidden to act or think a certain way, it only exacerbates your need to do so. January starts to find that she has inexplicable skills that help her when needed.<br /><br />One day she finds a strange book which talks of journeys between different worlds, mysterious doors, and ultimately, a love story, and she starts to see some similarities to things in her own life. But the more she tries to pursue these worlds, and find these doors, the more she is pursued, putting herself and those she cares about in grave danger.<br /><br />This is a pretty magical story about the ability to travel through time and different worlds. It’s the story of finding courage when you are at your most vulnerable, and realizing that our assumptions about how people feel about us can often be wrong.<br /><br />But as crazy as this story is, at its core it’s a love story, an adventure, a story of friendship, family, and how easy it is to fear the things we cannot understand. This book has memorable characters and is beautifully written. One trigger warning: there is some animal cruelty in the book, but it’s not a significant part of the book.<br /><br />I enjoyed <b>
  <i>The Ten Thousand Doors of January</i>
</b>, although I found it a bit confusing from time to time. It definitely requires you to suspend your disbelief. But if this type of book appeals to you it’s definitely worth the journey. <br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>.<br /><br />Check out my list of the best books I read in 2018 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html</a>. <br /><br />You can follow me on Instagram at <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener"> https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14010376624850245222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PsVyS6zaHoBW9XbUykyPk4Uqp1SliFx9RWJFtPZLiTYyrEim3HHtRvNLSd63NTA7sLwoWjNvwmWhboBPR32qcg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZFAT3o/nKda3nZiG++vMkSZEOL0AaY7dNkgImLWaitVoOSkz/0zaEBIjp4yGknM5E9K3s5aOEMXSRM1jBKypkQ==')})
  }
//]]>

  <span id="freeText9743292758547198892" style="display:none">a former academic, adjunct, cashier, and blueberry-harvester, Alix E. Harrow is now a full-time writer living in kentucky with her husband and their semi-feral kids. <br /><br />ahe is the author of hugo-award-winning short fiction, and her debut novel, THE TEN THOUSAND DOORS OF JANUARY (redhook/orbit 2019), was a finalist for the hugo, nebula, locus, world fantasy, and goodreads choice awards. her second book, THE ONCE AND FUTURE WITCHES, is out now! <br /><br />her writing is represented by Kate McKean at Howard Morhaim Literary Agency.<br /><br />newsletter: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://writtenworld.substack.com/">https://writtenworld.substack.com/</a><br />email: alixeharrow at gmail.com<br />twitter: AlixEHarrow<br />insta: alix.e.harrow</span>
